        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711548214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18120685554557320635">Wow. What a crazy, ambitious book. Definitely not the kind of book an author could write as a debut. It seems to me that there are a ton of books and films that spin off from this work, and it's indicative of Banks's wild and creative imagination that he was coming up with this kind of stuff before anyone else. I could find all sorts of elements of things to come: tinges of <em>Inception</em>, <em>The Matrix</em>, Alex Garland's <em>The Coma</em>, even the transcription of Scottish dialect that would turn up in Irvine Wel</span>
  <span id="freeText18120685554557320635" style="display:none">Wow. What a crazy, ambitious book. Definitely not the kind of book an author could write as a debut. It seems to me that there are a ton of books and films that spin off from this work, and it's indicative of Banks's wild and creative imagination that he was coming up with this kind of stuff before anyone else. I could find all sorts of elements of things to come: tinges of <em>Inception</em>, <em>The Matrix</em>, Alex Garland's <em>The Coma</em>, even the transcription of Scottish dialect that would turn up in Irvine Welsh's <em>Trainspotting</em> several years later.<br /><br />This was a tough book to get into, but I'm so glad I persevered. It became something enormous, something brilliant and breathtaking, like the giant structure of the bridge itself. <br /><br />I still get a bit sentimental reading Iain Banks. I ration his books, and have been trying not read them all -- even more so since he died. Reading this one, I thought how sad it was that he died so young (59), but then I feel happy when I read sections of books like this from the 80s, and see evidence of his ebullience back then -- a quality which I don't think he ever lost. I really hope he lived his life like this quote, and had no regrets when he died:<br /><br /><em>Damn it I wanna </em>do<em> things! I want to travel the Trans-Siberian, go to India, stand on Ayers Rock, get sodden wet in Machupicchu! I want to surf! I </em>will<em> get a hang-glider; I want to go back to the Grand Canyon and get further than just the rim rock this time, I want to see the aurora borealis from Svalbard or Greenland, I want to see a total eclipse, I want to watch pyroclastic displays, I want to walk inside a lava tunnel, I want to see the earth from space, I want to drink </em>chang<em> in Ladakh, I want to cruise down the Amazon and up the Yangtze and walk the Great Wall; I want to visit Azania! I want to watch them push helicopters off the aircraft carriers again! </em>I want to be in bed with three women at once!<br /><br />And here's a quote we can probably all relate to:<br /><br /><em>No, I don't know where I am.<br />No, I don't know who I am.<br />Yes of course I know it's all a dream.<br />Isn't everything?</em></span>
  <a data-text-id="18120685554557320635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_143037158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143037158?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2011</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143037158" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6977909993299787367">Having read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/567678.The_Wasp_Factory' title='The Wasp Factory by Iain M. Banks' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wasp Factory</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/422452.Against_a_Dark_Background' title='Against a Dark Background by Iain M. Banks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Against a Dark Background</a> I expected a lot from this book that had been sitting on my shelf for somewhere around 10 years. In someways I was disappointed but it was still a fairly enjoyable experience.<br/><br/>The sections on the bridge reminded me a lot of Kafka's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17689.Franz_Kafka_s_The_Castle__Dramatization_' title='Franz Kafka's The Castle (Dramatization) by David Fishelson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Castle</a> but better. The modern sections bored me (as most non-fantastic fiction does - with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/463.Philip_Roth' title='Philip Roth' rel='nofollow noopener'>Philip Roth</a> being the exception). The dreams were very cool, especially the trip to hell. Without the dreams the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText6977909993299787367" style="display:none">Having read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/567678.The_Wasp_Factory" title="The Wasp Factory by Iain M. Banks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wasp Factory</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/422452.Against_a_Dark_Background" title="Against a Dark Background by Iain M. Banks" rel="nofollow noopener">Against a Dark Background</a> I expected a lot from this book that had been sitting on my shelf for somewhere around 10 years. In someways I was disappointed but it was still a fairly enjoyable experience.<br /><br />The sections on the bridge reminded me a lot of Kafka's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17689.Franz_Kafka_s_The_Castle__Dramatization_" title="Franz Kafka's The Castle (Dramatization) by David Fishelson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Castle</a> but better. The modern sections bored me (as most non-fantastic fiction does - with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/463.Philip_Roth" title="Philip Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Philip Roth</a> being the exception). The dreams were very cool, especially the trip to hell. Without the dreams the book would have been a waste of time. Still I thought he could have dropped 40-50 pages to make it the perfect length. I didn't really enjoy the "off the bridge" part of the bridge sections.<br /><br />So I liked it but wouldn't really recommend it to anyone especially since Banks has a bunch of other books that are better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6977909993299787367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_116037108" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116037108" />
    <a title="Stevelvis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/832410-stevelvis"><img alt="Stevelvis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1292744743p2/832410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116037108?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stevelvis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stevelvis" href="/user/show/832410-stevelvis">Stevelvis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Banks fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stevelvis by: </span>
      Iain M. Banks
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116037108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8670098325101328352">The first half of this book was a good 4-5 stars as the strange surroundings, characters and events were weaving into a mysterious dystopic surreality. Half way through as the weave tightens the mystery and strangeness slowly fades into a reflection of everyday reality and a sort of biography of a Scots life through the 1970s-1980s.<br/><br/>I've already read all of Mr. Banks' more challenging novels of science fiction, all of which I've greatly enjoyed. The author has said that this is his favorite book </span>
  <span id="freeText8670098325101328352" style="display:none">The first half of this book was a good 4-5 stars as the strange surroundings, characters and events were weaving into a mysterious dystopic surreality. Half way through as the weave tightens the mystery and strangeness slowly fades into a reflection of everyday reality and a sort of biography of a Scots life through the 1970s-1980s.<br /><br />I've already read all of Mr. Banks' more challenging novels of science fiction, all of which I've greatly enjoyed. The author has said that this is his favorite book of those he's written and so my expectations may have been too high. I do recommend The Bridge, especially for Banks' fans, just don't expect a sci-fi masterpiece, and do enjoy the parts of it that are just that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8670098325101328352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94416006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4533649396217419659">Mostly very good. The problem I had with it was that there were several chapters told from a barbarian's veiwpoint and these pieces were all written in thick dialect. This slowed down the pace of the book to a crawl. (The only way he could have made it less enjoyable would be to have the dialect printed in italics.) I skipped every one of these chapters after slogging through the first and felt like I missed very little. There were some great set pieces and inventions in this book and it had som</span>
  <span id="freeText4533649396217419659" style="display:none">Mostly very good. The problem I had with it was that there were several chapters told from a barbarian's veiwpoint and these pieces were all written in thick dialect. This slowed down the pace of the book to a crawl. (The only way he could have made it less enjoyable would be to have the dialect printed in italics.) I skipped every one of these chapters after slogging through the first and felt like I missed very little. There were some great set pieces and inventions in this book and it had some truly funny Kafka-world comedy in it, as well (which I'm a sucker for).</span>
  <a data-text-id="4533649396217419659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119707482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13107750924923565569">One of my perennial favourites. I love the parallel world of the bridge and the way its details are seeded from the hero's life. Unfortunately there's a rough patch with some barbarians - why do most alternate-headworld novels seem to have a tedious section with a barbarian? The real-world strand hasn't stayed with me as much as the imaginative bravado of the bridge world, perhaps because I didn't have the feeling that the character had anything major to address. But I reread every few years for</span>
  <span id="freeText13107750924923565569" style="display:none">One of my perennial favourites. I love the parallel world of the bridge and the way its details are seeded from the hero's life. Unfortunately there's a rough patch with some barbarians - why do most alternate-headworld novels seem to have a tedious section with a barbarian? The real-world strand hasn't stayed with me as much as the imaginative bravado of the bridge world, perhaps because I didn't have the feeling that the character had anything major to address. But I reread every few years for pure enjoyment. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xCR/eBLehx/rbkXuIRDWpav5zfsMzwf4OvO2+iToidPwucLowTPisF++EDWhfBQF1ezjwxCWdThL2N3frp17TA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZeXC0V2I3fxNe/S5MaSMqXrb5Q1mrEDfpJpv0b+ZvR5ReH9BjmW4U/mroWKxyE4JBM7LNXr1Mh/VsQT0NexPgQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7628.Iain_Banks">About Iain Banks</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7628.Iain_Banks"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1374456581p3/7628.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7628.Iain_Banks">Iain Banks
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,397
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3596405646538811963">This author also published science fiction under the pseudonym <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5807106.Iain_M__Banks' title='Iain M. Banks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Iain M. Banks</a>.<br/><br/>Banks's father was an officer in the Admiralty and his mother was once a professional ice skater. Iain Banks was educated at the University of Stirling where he studied English Literature, Philosophy and Psychology. He moved to London and lived in the south of England until 1988 when he returned to Scotland, living in Edi</span>
  <span id="freeText3596405646538811963" style="display:none">This author also published science fiction under the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5807106.Iain_M__Banks" title="Iain M. Banks" rel="nofollow noopener">Iain M. Banks</a>.<br /><br />Banks's father was an officer in the Admiralty and his mother was once a professional ice skater. Iain Banks was educated at the University of Stirling where he studied English Literature, Philosophy and Psychology. He moved to London and lived in the south of England until 1988 when he returned to Scotland, living in Edinburgh and then Fife.<br /><br />Banks met his wife Annie in London, before the release of his first book. They married in Hawaii in 1982. However, he announced in early 2007 that, after 25 years together, they had separated. He lived most recently in North Queensferry, a town on the north side of the Firth of Forth near the Forth Bridge and the Forth Road Bridge.<br /><br />As with his friend Ken MacLeod (another Scottish writer of technical and social science fiction) a strong awareness of left-wing history shows in his writings. The argument that an economy of abundance renders anarchy and adhocracy viable (or even inevitable) attracts many as an interesting potential experiment, were it ever to become testable. He was a signatory to the Declaration of Calton Hill, which calls for Scottish independence.<br /><br />In late 2004, Banks was a prominent member of a group of British politicians and media figures who campaigned to have Prime Minister Tony Blair impeached following the 2003 invasion of Iraq. In protest he cut up his passport and posted it to 10 Downing Street. In an interview in Socialist Review he claimed he did this after he "abandoned the idea of crashing my Land Rover through the gates of Fife dockyard, after spotting the guys armed with machine guns." He related his concerns about the invasion of Iraq in his book <i>Raw Spirit</i>, and the principal protagonist (Alban McGill) in the novel <i>The Steep Approach to Garbadale</i> confronts another character with arguments in a similar vein.<br /><br />Interviewed on Mark Lawson's BBC Four series, first broadcast in the UK on 14 November 2006, Banks explained why his novels are published under two different names. His parents wished to name him Iain Menzies Banks but his father made a mistake when registering the birth and he was officially registered as Iain Banks. Despite this he continued to use his unofficial middle name and it was as Iain M. Banks that he submitted <i>The Wasp Factory</i> for publication. However, his editor asked if he would mind dropping the 'M' as it appeared "too fussy". The editor was also concerned about possible confusion with Rosie M. Banks, a minor character in some of P.G. Wodehouse's Jeeves novels who is a romantic novelist. After his first three mainstream novels his publishers agreed to publish his first SF novel, <i>Consider Phlebas</i>. To distinguish between the mainstream and SF novels, Banks suggested the return of the 'M', although at one stage he considered John B. Macallan as his SF pseudonym, the name deriving from his favourite whiskies: Johnnie Walker Black Label and The Macallan single malt.<br /><br />His latest book was a science fiction (SF) novel in the Culture series, called <i>The Hydrogen Sonata</i>, published in 2012.<br /><br />Author Iain M. Banks revealed in April 2013 that he had late-stage cancer. He died the following June.<br /><br />The Scottish writer posted a message on his official website saying his next novel <i>The Quarry</i>, due to be published later this year*, would be his last.<br /><br />* <i>The Quarry</i> was published in June 2013.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3596405646538811963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
